(TA.)    </entryFree>28:T10e6,<entryFree id="n37143" key="كَلَبٌ" type="main">     
                  <form>       
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">كَلَبٌ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form> (S, K) and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n37143-1" target="كُلَابٌ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n37149"/></foreign> (Lth) <hi rend="ital">Madness which affects a dog in consequence of eating human flesh.</hi> (K.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  Also, <hi rend="ital">Madness like that of dogs, which affects a man in consequence of his having been bitten by a</hi> [<hi rend="ital">mad</hi>] <hi rend="ital">dog:</hi> (K:) [<hi rend="ital">a disorder</hi>] <hi rend="ital">resembling madness,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">diobolical possession:</hi> (S:) <hi rend="ital">a disease that befalls a man from the bite of a mad dog, occasioning what resembles madness,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">diabolical possession, so that whomsoever he bites, that person also becomes in like manner affected, abstaining from drinking water until he dies of thirst:</hi> the Arabs concur in the assertion that its cure is a drop of the blood of a king, mixed with water, and given to the patient to drink. (TA.) Accord. to El-Mufaddal, it originates from a disease which befalls the standing corn &amp;c., and which is not removed until the sun rises upon it: if cattle eat of it before that, they die: wherefore Mohammad forbade pasturing by night: but sometimes a camel runs away, and eats of such pasture before sunrise, and dies in consequence: then a dog comes, and eats of its flesh, and becomes mad; and if it bite a man, he also becomes mad, and when he hears the barking of a dog, answers it [by barking]. (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">دِمَاءُ المُلُوكِ أَشْفَى مِنَ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">الكَلَبِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">The blood of kings has cured of canine madness</hi>]: or, accord. to another reading, <foreign lang="ar">دِمَاءُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">المُلُوكِ شِفَاءُ الكَلَبِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">The blood of kings is the cure for canine madness</hi>]. A proverb, explained by what is quoted from Lh, voce <foreign lang="ar">كَلِبٌ</foreign>. But some reject this explanation, and assert the meaning to be, that, when a man is enraged [by desire of obtaining revenge], and takes his blood revenge, the blood is the cure of his rage, though not really drunk. (TA.) See also <foreign lang="ar">كَلِبٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">كَلِبَ</foreign>.          <sense type="b" n="4">-b4-</sense>  [Also <foreign lang="ar">كَلَبٌ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">A madness like that of the dog, affecting camels.</hi> (See 4.)]          <sense type="b" n="5">-b5-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">كَلَبٌ</foreign> and
